جناية المملوك والجناية عليه
دفع سیده نصفه إلى الآخرين أو فداه بالدية، فإن قتل أحدهما عمدا، والآخر خطأ، أي سيد العبد أي نصف العبد الكاملة العبد أحد الزوجين فعفى أحد وليي العمد، فدى بالدية لوليي الخطأ، وبنصفها لأحد وليي العمد، المولى إن شاء أي وفدى أو دفعه إليهم أثلاثا عبدهما قتل قريبهما فعفى أحدهما بطل الكل. إن شاء العبد الأولياء الثلاثة الباقين أي الرجلين الرجلين وهما الوليان نصفه: يعني إذا قتل عبد رجلين عمدا، ولكل واحد من المقتولين وليان فعفا أحد وليي كل واحد من المقتولين، فالمولى بالخيار إن شاء دفع نصف العبد إلى الذي لم يعف من وليي القتيلين وإن شاء فداه بدية كاملة؛ لأن بذلك العفو سقط القصاص في الكل، وانقلب نصيب الساكتين مالا وهو دية كاملة؛ لأن كل واحد من القتيلين يجب له قصاص كامل على حدة، فإذا سقط القصاصان وجب أن ينقلب كله مالا وذلك ديتان، فيجب على المولى عشرون ألفا أو دفع العبد، غير أن نصيب العافيين سقط مجانا، فانقلب نصيب الساكتين مالا، وذلك دية واحدة لكل واحد منهما نصف الدية، أو دفع نصف العبد لهما، فيخير المولى بينهما. (عيني، فتح) إلى الآخرين وهما الوليان اللذان لم يعفوا. (عيني) فدى بالدية إلخ: أي المولى بالخيار، إن شاء فدى بالدية الكاملة لوليي الخطأ، وفدى بنصف الدية لأحد وليي العمد، وإن شاء دفعه إلى الأولياء الثلاثة أثلاثا، أما فداؤه بالدية لوليي الخطأ، وبنصفها لأحد وليي العمد، فلأن وليي الخطأ حقهما في الدابة عشرة آلاف درهم وحق وليي العمد في القصاص، فإذا عفا أحدهما انقلب نصيب الآخر مالا، وهو نصف الدية خمسة آلاف، فإذا فدى فداه بخمسة عشر ألف درهم عشرة آلاف لوليي الخطأ، وخمسة آلاف لغير العافي من وليي العمد، وأما دفعه أثلاثا أي من حيث الأثلاث، فيكون ثلثيه لوليي الخطأ، وثلثه للساكت من وليي العمد بطريق العول؛ لأن حقهم في الدية كذلك فيضرب وليا الخطأ بعشرة آلاف، ويضرب غير العافي من وليي العمد بخمسة آلاف وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما يدفعه أرباعا بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعه لوليي الخطأ، وربعه لغير العافي من وليي العمد؛ لأن نصفه سلم لوليي الخطأ بلا منازعة، واستوت منازعتهم في النصف الآخر، فينصف هذا حاصل ما في الفتح و"العيني" وغيرهما.
قريبهما: أي قريبا للرجلين كأبيهما وأخيهما. (عيني) بطل الكل معناه إن كان عبد بين رجلين، فقتل قريبا لهما كأمهما أو أخيهما، فعفا أحدهما بطل الجميع، ولا يستحق غير العافي منهما شيئا من العبد غير نصيبه الذي كان له من قبل، وكذا إذا كان العبد لقريب لهما أو لمعتقهما، فقتل مولاه فورثاه بطل الكل، هذا عند أبي حنيفة اليه، وقال أبو يوسف يدفع الذي عفا نصف نصيبه إلى الآخر إن شاء، وإن شاء فداه بربع الدية؛ لأن حق القصاص ثبت لهما في العبد على الشيوع؛ لأن الملك لا ينافي استحقاق القصاص عليه للمولى، فإذا عفا أحدهما انقلب نصيب الآخر وهو النصف مالا، غير أنه شائع في كل العبد، فيكون نصفه في نصيبه، ونصفه في نصيب صاحبه، فما أصاب نصيبه سقط؛ لأن المولى لا يستوجب على عبده مالا وما أصاب نصيب صاحبه ثبت، وهو نصف النصف، -
Book of Blood-Money. The injury of the slave and injury upon him. He (the master) pays half of him to the others or ransoms him with the full blood-money. If one of them killed intentionally and the other accidentally, i.e. the master of the slave, i.e. half of the slave, the complete blood-money, the slave, one of the two spouses. So if one of the two heirs of the intentional killing pardons, he ransoms with the blood-money for the two heirs of the accidental killing, and with half of it for one of the two heirs of the intentional killing. The master if he wishes, i.e. and he ransoms, or pays him to them in thirds. Their slave killed their relative and one of them pardoned, all is void. If he wishes the slave, the three remaining heirs, i.e. the two men, the two men and they are the two heirs. Half of it: meaning if a slave of two men kills intentionally, and for each of the two killed there are two heirs, and one of the two heirs of each of the killed pardons, then the master has the choice: if he wishes he hands over half of the slave to the one who did not pardon from among the two heirs of the two killed, and if he wishes he ransoms him with a complete blood-money; because by that pardon the retaliation is dropped completely, and the share of the silent ones turns into property, which is a complete blood-money; because for each of the two killed a complete retaliation is due separately, so when the two retaliations drop, it is necessary that it all turns into property, and that is two blood-monies, so the master owes twenty thousand or handing over the slave, except that the share of the two pardoners drops for free, so the share of the silent ones turns into property, and that is one blood-money for each of them half the blood-money, or handing over half the slave to them, so the master is given choice between them. ('Ayni, Fath) 'to the others' meaning the two heirs who did not pardon. ('Ayni) 'He ransoms with the blood-money etc.': i.e. the master has the choice: if he wishes he ransoms with the full blood-money for the two heirs of accidental killing, and ransoms with half the blood-money for one of the two heirs of intentional killing, and if he wishes he hands him over to the three heirs in thirds. As for his ransoming with the blood-money for the two heirs of accidental killing and with half of it for one of the two heirs of intentional killing, it is because the right of the two heirs of accidental killing is ten thousand dirhams in the blood-money, and the right of the two heirs of intentional killing is in retaliation, so when one of them pardons, the share of the other turns into property, which is half of the blood-money, five thousand. So if he ransoms, he ransoms with fifteen thousand dirhams: ten thousand for the two heirs of accidental killing and five thousand for the one who did not pardon among the two heirs of intentional killing. As for his handing over in thirds, i.e. from the aspect of thirds, so two-thirds is for the two heirs of accidental killing and one-third for the silent one among the two heirs of intentional killing by way of 'awl (proportional increase); because their right in the blood-money is like that. So the two heirs of accidental killing are given ten thousand, and the one who did not pardon among the two heirs of intentional killing is given five thousand. And this according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he hands over in fourths by way of munaza'ah (competition): three-fourths for the two heirs of accidental killing and one-fourth for the one who did not pardon among the two heirs of intentional killing; because half of it is yielded to the two heirs of accidental killing without competition, and their competition is equal in the other half, so it is halved. This is the summary of what is in al-Fath and al-'Ayni and others.
'Their relative': i.e. a relative of the two men like their father or brother. ('Ayni) 'All is void' means if a slave is owned by two men, and he kills a relative of theirs like their mother or brother, and one of them pardons, then all is void, and the one who did not pardon among them does not deserve anything of the slave except his own share that he had before. Similarly, if the slave is owned by a relative of theirs or by their freed slave, and he kills their master and they inherit him, then all is void. This according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: the one who pardoned pays half of his share to the other if he wishes, and if he wishes he ransoms it with one-fourth of the blood-money; because the right of retaliation for both of them in the slave is on joint ownership, because ownership does not preclude the entitlement of retaliation against him for the master. So when one of them pardons, the share of the other, which is half, turns into property, but it is common in the entire slave, so half of it is in his own share and half in his partner's share. What falls in his own share drops because the master does not owe property upon his slave, and what falls in his partner's share is established, which is half of half.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, with its commentary from 'Ayni and al-Fath, presents a complex case involving a slave and multiple victims with partial pardon. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute embedded within a ruling statement. The ruling: when a jointly-owned slave kills two victims—one intentionally, one accidentally—and one heir of each victim pardons, the master has two options: either pay the full blood-money (diyah) to the remaining heirs (10,000 to the accidental heirs, 5,000 to the intentional heir who didn't pardon) or hand over the slave in thirds (two-thirds to accidental heirs, one-third to intentional silent heir). This is Abu Hanifa's view. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ: they say the master hands over in fourths (three-fourths to accidental heirs, one-fourth to the intentional silent heir) based on the principle of munaza'ah (competition). The dispute arises because Abu Hanifa sees the rights as distinct, while the Sahibayn see the half shared. The passage also covers another scenario: if a slave jointly owned by two men kills a relative common to both (like their mother or brother) and one pardons, then according to Abu Hanifa the entire claim for retaliation drops and the non-pardoning heir gets nothing extra; Abu Yusuf allows him to receive compensation (half of his partner's share or a quarter diyah). The reasoning is that the right to retaliation was shared in the entire slave, and pardon extinguishes part, leaving only the part belonging to the pardoner's share automatically dropped.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional killing or injury.
العفو (al-'afw): Pardon by the heir, which drops qisas and may convert the right to property.
الدية (al-diyah): Blood-money paid as compensation for killing or injury.
العول (al-'awl): Proportional increase of denominators in inheritance to accommodate shares exceeding the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a jointly-owned slave killing two victims (one intentional, one accidental), and one heir of each pardons, how does Abu Hanifa say the master should divide the slave if he chooses to hand him over?
A) In fourths: 3/4 to accidental heirs, 1/4 to intentional silent heir
B) In thirds: 2/3 to accidental heirs, 1/3 to intentional silent heir
C) In halves: 1/2 to each set of heirs
D) The master pays full diyah and keeps the slave

Key Takeaway
When partial pardon occurs, the non-pardoning heirs' rights are converted to proportional claims on the slave's value, leading to an intra-Hanafi division dispute between thirds and fourths.

The Amount of Diyah for a Slave
Ruling with proof on the amount of diyah for a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the amount of compensation (diyah) owed for accidentally killing a male and a female slave under Hanafi law, and identify the threshold that triggers the cap.

Core Idea
The diyah for a slave is capped at 9,990 dirhams for a male and 4,990 dirhams for a female, reflecting the deficiency due to slavery.

In this passage, we learn the precise amounts of compensation for accidentally killing a slave. While the general rule is to pay the slave's market value, the Hanafi school imposes a maximum limit when the value reaches a certain threshold. This lesson focuses on the ruling itself and the specific numbers established by Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir clarifies the cap and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the obligation
The act under discussion is the accidental killing of a slave (qatl khata). The killer is obligated to pay compensation, known as diyah.
The obligation is wajib, not just recommended.
2
Determine the base rule for a male slave
If the slave's market value (qimah) is less than 10,000 dirhams, the killer must pay that value. If it is 10,000 dirhams or more, the payment is capped at 9,990 dirhams (10,000 minus 10).
The cap applies when the value equals or exceeds 10,000.
3
Determine the base rule for a female slave
If the female slave's value is less than 5,000 dirhams, her market value is paid. If it is 5,000 dirhams or more, the payment is capped at 4,990 dirhams (5,000 minus 10). There is also a narration stating a reduction of 5 dirhams.
The cap for a female slave is half that of a male slave, reflecting the general principle that a woman's diyah is half that of a man.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Abu Yusuf (one of the major disciples) holds that the full value should be paid without any cap, aligning with al-Shafi'i. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, which includes the cap.
The disagreement is based on different interpretations of the evidence.
5
Summarize the mufta bihi ruling
The operative ruling for fatwa: For a male slave, the maximum diyah is 9,990 dirhams; for a female slave, it is 4,990 dirhams. If the value is below these thresholds, the actual value is paid.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: لما فرغ من أحكام جناية العبد على غيره شرع في أحكام الجناية عليه؛ لأن الفاعل مقدم على المفعول وجودا. (فتح) قتل عبد خطأ إلخ : أي إذا قتل عبد قتلا خطأ تجب على القاتل قيمته إن لم تكن عشرة آلاف درهم، وإن كانت عشرة آلاف درهم، أو أكثر منها، ينقص منها أي من عشرة آلاف عشرة دراهم، فيقضى له بعشرة آلاف درهم إلا عشرة دراهم وفي الأمة إذا زادت قيمتها على خمسة آلاف أو تكون خمسة آلاف، الخمسة الآلاف عشرة دراهم، وفي رواية: ينقص خمسة دراهم، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: تجب قيمة العبد والمرأة بالغة ما بلغت؛ لما روي عن عمر وعلي وابن عمر الله أنهم أوجبوا في قتل العبد قيمته بالغة ما بلغت، ولأن الضمان باعتبار ماليته لا آدميته ولهذا تجب للمولى، وهو لا يملك إلا من حيث المالية، فصار كسائر الأموال، وللإمام ومحمد رحمها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ (النساء: ۹۲) وجه الاستدلال : أنه تعالى سمى الواجب في قتل المؤمن خطأ ،دية والعبد مؤمن قتل خطأ، فيجب فيه الدية، والدية اسم لما يجب بمقابلة الآدمي لا بمقابلة المال، فثبت بدلالة الآية أن العبد مضمون بمقابلة الآدمية، ولا يزاد على تقدير الشرع في الدبة، وينقص عنها بأثر عبد الله بن مسعود؛ لنقصان الرق فيه؛ لئلا يلزم التسوية بين الكامل والناقص، والدليل على أن معنى الآدمية راجح فيه: أن أكثر تكاليف الشرع متوجهة عليه بالإجماع من حيث الآدمية، ولهذا وجب القصاص بقتله بالإجماع مطلقا على قول أبي يوسف وفيما إذا كان القاتل عبدا عند الشافعي، وما روياه من الأثر معارض بأثر ابن مسعود. (فتح باختصار وغيره) نقص عشرة إلخ إشعارا بانحطاط درجة الرقيق عن الحر، وتعيين العشرة بأثر عبد الله بن مسعود ه "لا يبلغ بقيمة العبد دية الحر، وينقص منه عشرة دراهم"، والأثر في المقدرات كالخبر؛ إذ لا يعرف إلا سماعا، ولأن آدميته أنقص، فيكون بدلها أقل كالمرأة والجنين. (فتح) أو أكثر : معناه أن ينقص عشرة من عشرة آلاف، فإن كانت قيمته عشرة آلاف فقط، ينقص عشرة فقط، وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من عشرة آلاف ينقص ما زاد على عشرة آلاف، وينقص منها عشرة، وليس المراد أنه ينقص عشرة فقط، سواء كانت قيمته عشرة آلاف أو أكثر.
Section: When he finished from the rulings of injury of the slave upon others, he began the rulings of injury upon him, because the doer is given precedence over the done-to in existence. (Fath) 'If a slave is killed accidentally etc.': i.e. if a slave is killed accidentally, his value is obligatory upon the killer if it is not ten thousand dirhams. But if it is ten thousand dirhams or more, it is reduced from it, i.e. from ten thousand, by ten dirhams, so he is awarded ten thousand dirhams less ten dirhams. In the case of a female slave, if her value exceeds five thousand or is five thousand, [it is reduced] by ten dirhams, and in one narration: reduced by five dirhams. This is their view (Muhammad and Abu Yusuf?). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: The value of the male or female slave is obligatory whatever it reaches, based on reports from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that they obligated in killing a slave his value whatever it reached, and because the guarantee is based on his property value, not his humanity, and for this it is obligatory for the master, and he only owns from the financial aspect, so it becomes like other properties. Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) [relied on] the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And a blood-money delivered' (Qur'an 4:92). The way of inference: that He, exalted, named the obligatory in killing a believing man by mistake as blood-money, and the slave is a believer killed by mistake, so blood-money is obligatory for him, and blood-money is a name for what is obligatory in exchange for the human being, not in exchange for property. So it is established by the indication of the verse that the slave is guaranteed in exchange for his humanity, and it is not increased beyond the legal estimation in blood-money, and it is decreased from it by the effect of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, due to the deficiency of slavery in him, so that equality between the complete and the deficient is not necessitated. The evidence that the meaning of humanity is preponderant in him is that most of the legal obligations are addressed to him by consensus from the aspect of humanity, and for this reason retaliation is obligatory for killing him by consensus absolutely according to Abu Yusuf, and in the case where the killer is a slave according to al-Shafi'i. What they narrated of the effect is opposed by the effect of Ibn Mas'ud. (Fath, summarized and others) 'Reduced by ten etc.' is an indication of the low station of slaves compared to free persons, and the specification of ten is by the effect of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The value of a slave should not reach the blood-money of a free person, and it is reduced from it by ten dirhams.' The effect in estimated matters is like a hadith, since it is only known through hearing. And because his humanity is less, so his substitute is less, like the woman and the fetus. (Fath) 'Or more': meaning that ten is reduced from ten thousand. If his value is exactly ten thousand, only ten is reduced. If his value is more than ten thousand, what exceeds ten thousand is reduced, and ten is reduced from it. It is not meant that only ten is reduced whether the value is ten thousand or more.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, discussing the compensation (diyah) for accidentally killing a slave. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa (as stated 'cindahuma' likely referring to the two, though the text mentions Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i as opponents), if a slave is killed accidentally, the killer must pay the slave's value, but if that value is 10,000 dirhams or more, it is capped at 10,000 dirhams minus 10 dirhams. For a female slave, the cap is 5,000 dirhams minus 10 dirhams (or 5 dirhams in another narration). The basis is that a slave's diyah is like that of a free person but reduced due to the deficiency of slavery. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue for the full value regardless, citing practices of Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar, and stating that the guarantee is based on property value. The Hanafi response uses the Qur'anic verse 4:92 which calls compensation for killing a believer 'diyah'; a slave is a believer, so diyah applies, and diyah is a fixed amount for a human, not a property. The cap is established by the effect (athar) of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the slave's value should not reach the full diyah of a free person and is reduced by ten dirhams. The commentary also clarifies that if the value exceeds 10,000, the excess is waived and then an additional 10 is deducted, so the maximum payable is 9,990 dirhams.

Key Terms
الدية (al-diyah): The fixed compensation for killing a human being; for a free man it is 1000 dinars or 10,000 dirhams, and for a slave it is reduced.
الأثر (al-athar): A narration from a Companion, here the statement of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud regarding the value of a slave.
الرق (al-riqq): Slavery, which is a legal deficiency that reduces the compensation for killing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the maximum diyah for a male slave accidentally killed?
A) 10,000 dirhams exactly
B) 9,990 dirhams
C) The full market value
D) 5,000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The diyah for a slave is capped at 9,990 dirhams for a male and 4,990 dirhams for a female, reflecting the deficiency of slavery.

Diyat — Blood Money

The Evidence for the Cap on a Slave's Diyah
Proof analysis: Qur'an and athar for the cap on slave diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two key proofs (Qur'an and athar) used by Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad to justify the cap on a slave's diyah, and explain how they counter the opposing view.

Core Idea
The cap on a slave's diyah is proven by the Qur'anic designation of diyah for a human and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud reducing it by ten dirhams.

This lesson delves into the evidence behind the Hanafi ruling on a slave's diyah. While the previous lesson focused on the amounts, here we examine the proof structure: how the Qur'anic verse (4:92) establishes that compensation for a slave is a diyah (a human‑based payment) and how the athar of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud sets the exact reduction. We also see the rebuttal to the opposing view of Abu Yusuf and al‑Shafiʻi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main proofs
The passage presents two primary proofs for the cap: the Qur'anic verse (4:92) and the athar (effect) of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The verse shows the slave's compensation is a diyah, which is a fixed amount for a human; the athar provides the specific reduction of ten dirhams.
The athar is treated like a hadith in estimated matters.
2
Analyze the Qur'anic proof (wajh al-dalalah)
Qur'an 4:92 calls the compensation for killing a mu'min (believer) by mistake 'diyah'. A slave is a mu'min, so his compensation is also a diyah. Diyah is a term used for compensation in exchange for humanity (ādamīyah), not property. Therefore, the slave's compensation cannot be open‑ended property value; it must be a fixed amount, like the diyah of a free person, but reduced due to slavery.
The verse uses the word 'diyah' generically; the Hanafi derive that it must be a fixed amount.
3
Examine the athar of Ibn Mas'ud
The athar states: 'The value of a slave should not reach the diyah of a free person, and it is reduced from it by ten dirhams.' This sets the specific reduction of ten dirhams from the free diyah (10,000 dirhams), resulting in 9,990. The commentary notes that in estimated matters (muqaddarāt), the athar is as strong as a hadith because it is only known through hearing (samāʻan).
The athar is a Companion statement, which in Hanafi usul is considered proof when no hadith exists.
4
Understand the rebuttal to the opposing view
Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue based on reports from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar that the slave's full value should be paid, treating the slave as property. The Hanafi response is that those reports are countered by the athar of Ibn Mas'ud, which is more specific. Additionally, the slave's humanity (ādamīyah) is dominant because he is subject to most Sharia obligations (taklif), so he is not like other property.
The principle that a slave is both a human and property, but his humanity prevails for diyah purposes.
5
Synthesize the full proof chain
The complete Hanafi proof: (1) Qur'an 4:92 establishes that the slave's compensation is a diyah, a human‑based fixed amount. (2) The free diyah is 10,000 dirhams. (3) The athar of Ibn Mas'ud reduces it by 10 dirhams due to slavery. (4) Therefore, the diyah for a male slave is 9,990 dirhams. (5) For a female, the free diyah is 5,000, reduced by 10 (or 5) to 4,990 (or 4,995).
This chain combines textual and rational elements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: لما فرغ من أحكام جناية العبد على غيره شرع في أحكام الجناية عليه؛ لأن الفاعل مقدم على المفعول وجودا. (فتح) قتل عبد خطأ إلخ : أي إذا قتل عبد قتلا خطأ تجب على القاتل قيمته إن لم تكن عشرة آلاف درهم، وإن كانت عشرة آلاف درهم، أو أكثر منها، ينقص منها أي من عشرة آلاف عشرة دراهم، فيقضى له بعشرة آلاف درهم إلا عشرة دراهم وفي الأمة إذا زادت قيمتها على خمسة آلاف أو تكون خمسة آلاف، الخمسة الآلاف عشرة دراهم، وفي رواية: ينقص خمسة دراهم، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: تجب قيمة العبد والمرأة بالغة ما بلغت؛ لما روي عن عمر وعلي وابن عمر الله أنهم أوجبوا في قتل العبد قيمته بالغة ما بلغت، ولأن الضمان باعتبار ماليته لا آدميته ولهذا تجب للمولى، وهو لا يملك إلا من حيث المالية، فصار كسائر الأموال، وللإمام ومحمد رحمها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ (النساء: ۹۲) وجه الاستدلال : أنه تعالى سمى الواجب في قتل المؤمن خطأ ،دية والعبد مؤمن قتل خطأ، فيجب فيه الدية، والدية اسم لما يجب بمقابلة الآدمي لا بمقابلة المال، فثبت بدلالة الآية أن العبد مضمون بمقابلة الآدمية، ولا يزاد على تقدير الشرع في الدبة، وينقص عنها بأثر عبد الله بن مسعود؛ لنقصان الرق فيه؛ لئلا يلزم التسوية بين الكامل والناقص، والدليل على أن معنى الآدمية راجح فيه: أن أكثر تكاليف الشرع متوجهة عليه بالإجماع من حيث الآدمية، ولهذا وجب القصاص بقتله بالإجماع مطلقا على قول أبي يوسف وفيما إذا كان القاتل عبدا عند الشافعي، وما روياه من الأثر معارض بأثر ابن مسعود. (فتح باختصار وغيره) نقص عشرة إلخ إشعارا بانحطاط درجة الرقيق عن الحر، وتعيين العشرة بأثر عبد الله بن مسعود ه "لا يبلغ بقيمة العبد دية الحر، وينقص منه عشرة دراهم"، والأثر في المقدرات كالخبر؛ إذ لا يعرف إلا سماعا، ولأن آدميته أنقص، فيكون بدلها أقل كالمرأة والجنين. (فتح) أو أكثر : معناه أن ينقص عشرة من عشرة آلاف، فإن كانت قيمته عشرة آلاف فقط، ينقص عشرة فقط، وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من عشرة آلاف ينقص ما زاد على عشرة آلاف، وينقص منها عشرة، وليس المراد أنه ينقص عشرة فقط، سواء كانت قيمته عشرة آلاف أو أكثر.
Section: When he finished from the rulings of injury of the slave upon others, he began the rulings of injury upon him, because the doer is given precedence over the done-to in existence. (Fath) 'If a slave is killed accidentally etc.': i.e. if a slave is killed accidentally, his value is obligatory upon the killer if it is not ten thousand dirhams. But if it is ten thousand dirhams or more, it is reduced from it, i.e. from ten thousand, by ten dirhams, so he is awarded ten thousand dirhams less ten dirhams. In the case of a female slave, if her value exceeds five thousand or is five thousand, [it is reduced] by ten dirhams, and in one narration: reduced by five dirhams. This is their view (Muhammad and Abu Yusuf?). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: The value of the male or female slave is obligatory whatever it reaches, based on reports from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that they obligated in killing a slave his value whatever it reached, and because the guarantee is based on his property value, not his humanity, and for this it is obligatory for the master, and he only owns from the financial aspect, so it becomes like other properties. Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) [relied on] the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And a blood-money delivered' (Qur'an 4:92). The way of inference: that He, exalted, named the obligatory in killing a believing man by mistake as blood-money, and the slave is a believer killed by mistake, so blood-money is obligatory for him, and blood-money is a name for what is obligatory in exchange for the human being, not in exchange for property. So it is established by the indication of the verse that the slave is guaranteed in exchange for his humanity, and it is not increased beyond the legal estimation in blood-money, and it is decreased from it by the effect of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, due to the deficiency of slavery in him, so that equality between the complete and the deficient is not necessitated. The evidence that the meaning of humanity is preponderant in him is that most of the legal obligations are addressed to him by consensus from the aspect of humanity, and for this reason retaliation is obligatory for killing him by consensus absolutely according to Abu Yusuf, and in the case where the killer is a slave according to al-Shafi'i. What they narrated of the effect is opposed by the effect of Ibn Mas'ud. (Fath, summarized and others) 'Reduced by ten etc.' is an indication of the low station of slaves compared to free persons, and the specification of ten is by the effect of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The value of a slave should not reach the blood-money of a free person, and it is reduced from it by ten dirhams.' The effect in estimated matters is like a hadith, since it is only known through hearing. And because his humanity is less, so his substitute is less, like the woman and the fetus. (Fath) 'Or more': meaning that ten is reduced from ten thousand. If his value is exactly ten thousand, only ten is reduced. If his value is more than ten thousand, what exceeds ten thousand is reduced, and ten is reduced from it. It is not meant that only ten is reduced whether the value is ten thousand or more.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, discussing the compensation (diyah) for accidentally killing a slave. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa (as stated 'cindahuma' likely referring to the two, though the text mentions Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i as opponents), if a slave is killed accidentally, the killer must pay the slave's value, but if that value is 10,000 dirhams or more, it is capped at 10,000 dirhams minus 10 dirhams. For a female slave, the cap is 5,000 dirhams minus 10 dirhams (or 5 dirhams in another narration). The basis is that a slave's diyah is like that of a free person but reduced due to the deficiency of slavery. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue for the full value regardless, citing practices of Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar, and stating that the guarantee is based on property value. The Hanafi response uses the Qur'anic verse 4:92 which calls compensation for killing a believer 'diyah'; a slave is a believer, so diyah applies, and diyah is a fixed amount for a human, not a property. The cap is established by the effect (athar) of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the slave's value should not reach the full diyah of a free person and is reduced by ten dirhams. The commentary also clarifies that if the value exceeds 10,000, the excess is waived and then an additional 10 is deducted, so the maximum payable is 9,990 dirhams.

Key Terms
الدية (al-diyah): The fixed compensation for killing a human being; for a free man it is 1000 dinars or 10,000 dirhams, and for a slave it is reduced.
الأثر (al-athar): A narration from a Companion, here the statement of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud regarding the value of a slave.
وجه الاستدلال (wajh al-istidlāl): The way of inference from a textual proof; the method by which the ruling is derived from the verse or hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It specifies the exact amount of 9,990 dirhams.
B) It establishes that the slave's compensation is a diyah (human‑based payment), not property value.
C) It contradicts the athar of Ibn Mas'ud.
D) It supports the view of Abu Yusuf.

Key Takeaway
The slave's diyah cap is derived from the Qur'anic concept of diyah (human‑based) and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud setting the reduction.

Compensation for Unintentional Killing of a Slave
Ruling on compensation for accidental killing of a slave with deduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for accidentally killing a slave, explain the evidence from Quran and athar, and evaluate the disagreement with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A slave's accidental killing is compensated by his value, but capped by the diyah of a free man and reduced by ten dirhams, affirming his human dignity over mere property.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary Fath al-Qadir presents the Hanafi ruling on diyah for a slave. It is a case where the human aspect (adamīyah) of the slave is weighed against his property aspect (māliyah). The ruling is based on the Quranic term 'diyah' and an athar from Ibn Mas'ud, and it involves an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the accidental killing (qatl khaṭa') of a slave. The ruling is that the killer must pay the slave's value (qīmah), but with a cap: for a male slave, if the value is 10,000 dirhams or more, only 9,990 is due; for a female, if 5,000 or more, 4,990 (or 4,995 in a narration).
The hukm level is wājib, a financial penalty.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main evidence is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa 4:92) which uses the word 'diyah' for compensation of a believer killed by mistake. The slave is a believer, so the compensation is called diyah, which is a payment for the human aspect, not just property value.
The term 'diyah' indicates a fixed measure tied to humanity.
3
Understand the deduction via athar
The specific amount (10 dirhams deduction from 10,000) is derived from the athar of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, which states that a slave's value does not reach the diyah of a free person and ten dirhams are deducted from it. This athar is treated like a prophetic report (khabar) in matters of fixed quantities.
The deduction signifies the lower rank of slaves, just as a woman's diyah is half.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Abu Yusuf (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the full market value must be paid without any cap. They rely on reports from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Umar that they obligated full value, and argue that the slave's compensation is purely based on property value (māliyah).
The dispute is about whether the human aspect or property aspect dominates.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) prefers the capped view. The Quranic verse and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud are given weight. The reports from Umar et al. are considered weak in comparison. The mufta bihi opinion is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The practical difference (thamarah): a slave worth 100,000 dirhams would only cost 9,990 dirhams under the Hanafi view, but full 100,000 under the opposing view.

Source Text

فصل قتل عبد خطأ تجب قيمته، ونقص عشرة لو كانت عشرة آلاف أو أكثر، أي ولكن نقص قیمته درهم وهو الربع، فيدفع نصف نصيبه، أو يفديه بربع الدية، ولأبي حنيفة أن ما يجب من المال يكون حق المولى؛ لأنه بدل دمه ولهذا يقضى منه ديونه وتنفذ منه وصاياه ثم الورثة يخلفونه فيه عند الفراغ من حاجته، والمولى لا يستوجب على عبده مالا فلا تخلفه الورثة فيه ولأن القصاص لما صار مالا صار بمعنى الخطأ، وفيه لا يجب شيء، فكذا ما هو في معنى ذلك تكملة البحر الرائق: ٢٢٥/٩] فصل: لما فرغ من أحكام جناية العبد على غيره شرع في أحكام الجناية عليه؛ لأن الفاعل مقدم على المفعول وجودا. (فتح) قتل عبد خطأ إلخ : أي إذا قتل عبد قتلا خطأ تجب على القاتل قيمته إن لم تكن عشرة آلاف درهم، وإن كانت عشرة آلاف درهم، أو أكثر منها، ينقص منها أي من عشرة آلاف عشرة دراهم، فيقضى له بعشرة آلاف درهم إلا عشرة دراهم وفي الأمة إذا زادت قيمتها على خمسة آلاف أو تكون خمسة آلاف، الخمسة الآلاف عشرة دراهم، وفي رواية: ينقص خمسة دراهم، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي: تجب قيمة العبد والمرأة بالغة ما بلغت؛ لما روي عن عمر وعلي وابن عمر الله أنهم أوجبوا في قتل العبد قيمته بالغة ما بلغت، ولأن الضمان باعتبار ماليته لا آدميته ولهذا تجب للمولى، وهو لا يملك إلا من حيث المالية، فصار كسائر الأموال، وللإمام ومحمد رحمها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَدِيَةٌ مُسَلَّمَةٌ (النساء: ۹۲) وجه الاستدلال : أنه تعالى سمى الواجب في قتل المؤمن خطأ دية والعبد مؤمن قتل خطأ، فيجب فيه الدية، والدية اسم لما يجب بمقابلة الآدمي لا بمقابلة المال، فثبت بدلالة الآية أن العبد مضمون بمقابلة الآدمية، ولا يزاد على تقدير الشرع في الدبة، وينقص عنها بأثر عبد الله بن مسعود؛ لنقصان الرق فيه؛ لئلا يلزم التسوية بين الكامل والناقص، والدليل على أن معنى الآدمية راجح فيه: أن أكثر تكاليف الشرع متوجهة عليه بالإجماع من حيث الآدمية، ولهذا وجب القصاص بقتله بالإجماع مطلقا على قول أبي يوسف وفيما إذا كان القاتل عبدا عند الشافعي، وما روياه من الأثر معارض بأثر ابن مسعود. (فتح باختصار وغيره) نقص عشرة إلخ إشعارا بانحطاط درجة الرقيق عن الحر، وتعيين العشرة بأثر عبد الله بن مسعود ه "لا يبلغ بقيمة العبد دية الحر، وينقص منه عشرة دراهم"، والأثر في المقدرات كالخبر؛ إذ لا يعرف إلا سماعا، ولأن آدميته أنقص، فيكون بدلها أقل كالمرأة والجنين. (فتح) أو أكثر : معناه أن ينقص عشرة من عشرة آلاف، فإن كانت قيمته عشرة آلاف فقط، ينقص عشرة فقط، وإن كانت قيمته أكثر من عشرة آلاف ينقص ما زاد على عشرة آلاف، وينقص منها عشرة، وليس المراد أنه ينقص عشرة فقط، سواء كانت قيمته عشرة آلاف أو أكثر.
A chapter: If a slave is killed by mistake, his value is obligatory, and it is reduced by ten if it is ten thousand or more, meaning but the reduction of his value is a dirham which is a quarter, so he pays half of his share, or ransoms him with a quarter of the diyah. According to Abu Hanifa, what is obligatory of wealth is the right of the master, because it is in exchange for his blood, and therefore his debts are paid from it and his bequests are executed. Then the heirs succeed him in it after his needs are fulfilled, and the master does not owe his slave any wealth, so the heirs do not succeed him in it. And because when retaliation becomes wealth, it becomes in the sense of error, and in error nothing is obligatory, so likewise what is in that sense. (Completion of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 9:225) A chapter: When he finished the rulings of the slave's aggression against others, he began the rulings of aggression against him, because the doer is prior to the object in existence. (Fath) 'Killing a slave by mistake, etc.': that is, if a slave is killed by mistake, the value is obligatory on the killer if it is not ten thousand dirhams; and if it is ten thousand dirhams or more, ten dirhams are deducted from it, i.e. from ten thousand, so he is awarded ten thousand dirhams minus ten dirhams. And for the female slave, if her value increases above five thousand or is five thousand, from five thousand [deduct] ten dirhams, and in a narration: deduct five dirhams, and this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: The value of the male slave and the woman is obligatory whatever it reaches, due to what was narrated from 'Umar, 'Ali, and Ibn 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, that they obligated the value of a slave for his killing whatever it reached. And because the guarantee is based on his property value not his humanity, and therefore it is owed to the master, and he only owns from the perspective of property, so it becomes like other property. And for the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And a diyah handed over' (al-Nisa 4:92). The aspect of deduction: that Allah the Exalted named the obligatory in killing a believer by mistake as diyah, and the slave is a believer killed by mistake, so diyah is obligatory for him. And diyah is a name for what is obligatory in exchange for the human being, not in exchange for property. So it is proven by the indication of the verse that the slave is guaranteed in exchange for his humanity, and it does not exceed the legal estimate for diyah, and it is reduced due to the athar of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, due to the deficiency of slavery in him, so that equality between the perfect and the deficient does not become necessary. And the evidence that the meaning of humanity is preponderant in him is that most of the legal obligations are directed at him by consensus from the perspective of humanity, and therefore retaliation is obligatory for killing him by consensus absolutely according to Abu Yusuf, and when the killer is a slave according to al-Shafi'i. And what they narrated from the athar is contradicted by the athar of Ibn Mas'ud. (Fath abridged and others) 'Reduction of ten, etc.' indicates the lowness of the rank of slaves compared to free persons, and the specification of ten is by the athar of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: 'The value of a slave does not reach the diyah of a free person, and ten dirhams are deducted from it.' And the athar in matters of estimates is like a report, because it is only known through hearing. And because his humanity is deficient, so its compensation is less, like the woman and the fetus. (Fath) 'Or more' means that ten is deducted from ten thousand. If his value is exactly ten thousand, only ten is deducted; if his value is more than ten thousand, what exceeds ten thousand is deducted, and ten is deducted from it. It does not mean that only ten is deducted whether his value is ten thousand or more.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and athar regarding the compensation for accidentally killing a slave. The author of Fath al-Qadir (Ibn al-Humam) explains the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq. The basic ruling: if a slave is killed by mistake, the killer must pay the slave's value (qimah). However, the value is capped: if the slave's value is 10,000 dirhams or more, only 10 dirhams are deducted and the killer pays 9,990 dirhams. For a female slave, the cap is 5,000 dirhams minus 10 (or 5 in one narration). This is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani). Abu Yusuf (in disagreement with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and al-Shafi'i hold that full value must be paid regardless of amount. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) relies on the verse of diyah (4:92) which calls the compensation for killing a believer 'diyah', even if the victim is a slave, so the slave's compensation is diyah (tied to humanity) not mere property value. Since diyah is fixed at 10,000 dirhams for a free person, the slave's must be less due to the defect of slavery, as indicated by the athar of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The value of a slave does not reach the diyah of a free person; rather ten dirhams are deducted from it.' This reduction signifies the lower status of slaves. The text also clarifies that if the value exceeds 10,000, the excess is deducted along with the fixed 10, so the total payable is always 9,990 for a male slave above the cap. The female slave's cap is 5,000 minus 10 (or 5). The commentary notes that this is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Compensation paid for killing a person by mistake, measured in terms of human value (300 dirhams or 20 camels etc. for a free person).
قيمة (qimah): Market value of a slave as property, used to determine compensation.
أثر (athar): A narration from a Companion (here Ibn Mas'ud) considered as a source of law in the Hanafi school, especially for estimates.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the maximum compensation for accidentally killing a male slave whose market value is 15,000 dirhams?
A) 15,000 dirhams
B) 10,000 dirhams minus 10 = 9,990 dirhams
C) 10,000 dirhams
D) 5,000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school compensates the accidental killing of a slave with his value, but capped at 9,990 dirhams for a male and 4,990 for a female, affirming the human aspect alongside property.

Compensation for Cutting a Slave's Hand: The Hanafi Cap Principle
Compensation for a slave's hand with cap and rebuttal of opposing view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for compensation for a slave's hand and explain the reasoning behind the proportional cap.

Core Idea
A slave's hand is compensated at half his value, capped proportionally to prevent absurdity.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on financial compensation for cutting a slave's hand. The key principle is that compensation is half the slave's value but subject to a proportional cap derived from the free person's diyah and the overall cap on a slave's value. We will contrast this with the opposing view that treats limbs as property without a cap.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
State that for cutting a slave's hand, the compensation is half the slave's value.
The source says 'ففي يده نصف قيمته'.
2
Understand the cap
The compensation cannot exceed 5,000 dirhams minus 5 for a male slave, proportional to the whole cap (10,000 - 10).
The text reads 'لا يزاد على خمسة آلاف إلا خمسة'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument
Since the hand is half the human body in diyah, it is half the slave's value. The cap ensures consistency with the whole cap.
The source says 'اليد في الآدمي نصفه فيعتبر بكله'.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
Malik and Ahmad treat limbs as property and give full proportional value without cap. The Hanafi reject this because it leads to absurdity: a hand cut could be worth more than killing the slave.
Example: slave worth 100,000, hand compensation 50,000 vs. killing 9,990.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The cap principle is the relied-upon view in major works like al-Hidayah.
Source: 'ما ذكره الشيخ العيني أولا ورجحه هو الذي جزم به الملتقي'.

وما قدر من العبد المغصوب بالإجماع دية الحر قدر من قيمته ففي يده نصف قيمته. ففي يده إلخ: توضيح للحكم المذكور أي إذا كان ما قدر من دية الحر مقدرا من قيمة العبد، ففي قطع يده يجب نصف قيمته، لا يزاد على خمسة آلاف إلا خمسة؛ لأن اليد في الآدمي نصفه فيعتبر بكله، وينقص هذا المقدار إظهارا لدناءة مرتبته، وقيل: يضمن في الأطراف بحسابه بالغة ما بلغت، ولا ينقص منه شيء؛ لأن الأطراف يسلك فيها مسلك الأموال، وهو قول مالك وأحمد في رواية إلا في الآمة والجائفة والمنقلة والموضحة فيقدر فيها ما يقدر في دية الحر، وهذا أمر شنيع؛ لأنه إذا كانت قيمته مثلا مائة ألف فإنه بقطع يده يجب خمسون ألفا، وبقتله عشرة آلاف إلا عشرة. [ رمز الحقائق ٤٦١/٢] أقول: ما ذكره الشيخ العيني أولا، ورجحه هو الذي جزم به الملتقي، وأخذه في عامة الكتب "كـ الهداية" و"الخلاصة" و"مجمع البحرين" وغيرها، وما ذكره ثانيا وضيفه هو الذي صححه بعضهم، وهو ظاهر الرواية، والتفصيل في "رد المحتار". قطع يد عبد الخ: اعلم أن قطع يد العبد لا يخلو إما أن يكون عمدا أو خطأ، وكل وجه على وجهين، إما أن يكون للعبد وارث غير السيد أو لم يكن، فإن كان القطع عمدا ووارثه غيره، فالإعتاق يقطع السراية إجماعا، ولا يجب القصاص، وإن لم يكن له ورثة لا يقطع السراية عندهما خلافا لمحمد، وإن كان القطع خطأ، فالإعتاق يقطع السراية إجماعا، سواء كان له وارث أم لا، ولا تجب القيمة والدية، بل يجب نقصان القيمة بالقطع. (فتح) لا يقتص: أي لا يقتص القاطع بالإجماع؛ لاشتباه من له الحق؛ لأن القصاص يجب عند الموت مستندا إلى وقت الجرح، فعلى اعتبار حالة الجرح يكون الحق للمولى، وعلى اعتبار الحالة الثانية يكون للورثة، فتحقق الاشتباه، فسقط القصاص رمز الحقائق : ٤٦١/٢] وإلا اقتص منه : يعني وإن لم يكن للعبد ورثة غير السيد اقتص منه أي من القاطع عندهما، وقال محمد: لا يجب القصاص هنا أيضا ؛ لاختلاف سبب الولاية؛ لأن الملك على اعتبار حالة الجرح، والوراثة بالولاء على اعتبار حالة الموت فنزل اختلاف السبب منزلة اختلاف المستحق، فتمكنت الشبهة، فسقط القصاص، ولهما التيقن بثبوت الولاية للمولى، فيستوفيه [رمز الحقائق: ٤٦١/٢]
And whatever is determined from the usurped slave by consensus as the diyah of a free person, from his value, so for his hand it is half his value. (Commentary) 'So for his hand, etc.' is a clarification of the mentioned ruling: that if what is determined from the diyah of a free person is determined from the value of the slave, then for cutting his hand, half his value is obligatory, and it is not increased beyond five thousand except five, because the hand of a human is half of him, so it is considered by the whole, and this amount is reduced to show the lowness of his rank. And it is said: he is liable for limbs in proportion whatever it reaches, and nothing is deducted from it, because limbs are treated as property; this is the view of Malik and Ahmad in one narration, except for the umm walad, the penetrating wound, the head-wound exposing bone, and the wound exposing the skull, for which the same as the diyah of a free person is determined. And this is an abominable matter, because if his value is, for example, one hundred thousand, then for cutting his hand fifty thousand is obligatory, and for killing him ten thousand minus ten. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:461). I say: What al-'Ayni mentioned first and preferred is what al-Multaqi affirmed and took in most books like al-Hidayah, al-Khulasa, Majma' al-Bahrain, etc. And what he mentioned second and added is what some scholars declared correct, and it is the apparent position in the narration, and the details are in Radd al-Muhtar. 'Cutting the hand of a slave, etc.': Know that cutting the hand of a slave is either intentional or by mistake, and each aspect has two aspects: either the slave has an heir other than the master, or he does not. If the cutting is intentional and his heir is other than the master, then emancipation cuts off the progression by consensus, and retaliation is not obligatory. If he has no heirs, the progression is not cut off according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani). If the cutting is by mistake, then emancipation cuts off the progression by consensus, whether he has an heir or not, and the value and diyah are not obligatory; rather the decrease in value due to the cutting is obligatory. (Fath) 'He is not retaliated against': meaning the cutter is not subjected to retaliation by consensus, due to confusion as to who holds the right, because retaliation becomes obligatory at death based on the time of the wound. Considering the time of the wound, the right belongs to the master; considering the second state (at death), it belongs to the heirs. So confusion arises, and retaliation falls. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:461) 'Otherwise he is retaliated against': meaning if the slave has no heir other than the master, the cutter is retaliated against according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said: Retaliation is not obligatory here either, due to the difference in the cause of authority, because ownership is based on the time of the wound, and inheritance by wala' is based on the time of death. So the difference in cause is considered like difference in the entitled party, so doubt prevails, and retaliation falls. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), certainty of the master's authority is established, so he executes it. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 2:461)
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated issues: (1) the proportion of compensation for cutting a limb of a slave, and (2) the effect of emancipation after a wound and before death on retaliation (qisas) and financial compensation. The first part discusses the principle that for a slave, compensation for limbs is proportional to the value of the whole slave. Since the hand is half the body in terms of diyah for a free person (half of 10,000 = 5,000), for a slave it is half the value. But there is a cap: the half cannot exceed 5,000 minus 5? Actually the text says 'لا يزاد على خمسة آلاف إلا خمسة' meaning it is not increased beyond 5,000 except by five? This seems to mirror the cap on the whole (10,000-10 for male; 5,000-5 for female). So the hand's compensation is half the value but capped proportionally. There is an alternative view (of Malik and Ahmad) that limbs are treated as property and full proportional value is paid without reduction, but the Hanafi school rejects this as leading to absurd results (e.g., cutting a hand of a slave worth 100,000 would give 50,000, but killing the same slave gives only 9,990). The Hanafi position is that the limb compensation follows the same logic as the whole (capped). The second part discusses the scenario: a slave's hand is cut (intentionally or by mistake), then the master emancipates the slave, and then the slave dies from the wound. The ruling on retaliation depends on whether the slave had an heir other than the master. If the cut was intentional and the slave has another heir, emancipation stops the progression (sarāyah) of the wound by consensus, so if the slave dies later, no retaliation (qisas) is due because the right of the master (who owned the slave at the time of wound) is superseded by the heirs, but there is confusion. If the slave has no other heir (i.e., the master is the sole heir by wala'), then according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the progression is not cut off and retaliation is possible (since the master is the same person who owned the slave and now inherits him). Muhammad (al-Shaybani) dissents: he says no retaliation because the cause of right changes (ownership at wound vs. inheritance at death), creating doubt. If the cut was by mistake, emancipation always cuts off progression by consensus, and only the decrease in value due to the cut is owed (not the full value). The commentary by Ramz al-Haqa'iq cites the relevant authorities.

Key Terms
سراية (sarāyah): Progression of an injury leading to death; the effect of the wound extending over time to cause death.
قصاص (qisās): Retaliation in kind for intentional injury or killing.
دية (diyah): Blood money or financial compensation for homicide or bodily injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the compensation for cutting the hand of a male slave worth 15,000 dirhams?
A) 7,500 dirhams
B) 5,000 dirhams
C) 4,995 dirhams
D) 7,500 dirhams minus 5

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school caps limb compensation for a slave to avoid absurdity, using qiyas from the whole slave's cap.

Effect of Emancipation on Retaliation (Qisas) for a Slave's Injury
Rulings on sarayah and qisas after emancipation with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on progression (sarayah) and retaliation when a slave is emancipated after injury and then dies.

Core Idea
Emancipation after injury cuts progression by mistake, but for intentional injury with no heir, the majority holds progression continues and qisas applies.

This lesson addresses the complex scenario where a slave's hand is cut, the master emancipates him, and the slave then dies from the wound. The rulings differ based on whether the injury was intentional or mistaken, and whether the slave has an heir other than the master. We will examine the positions of the Hanafi imams, including an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf/Muhammad and Muhammad al-Shaybani alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Cases are defined by two factors: intentional vs. mistaken, and presence of an heir other than master vs. no other heir.
The text says 'إما أن يكون عمدا أو خطأ، وكل وجه على وجهين'.
2
Scenario 1: intentional + other heir
Emancipation cuts progression by consensus; no qisas.
Source: 'فإن كان القطع عمدا ووارثه غيره، فالإعتاق يقطع السراية إجماعا، ولا يجب القصاص'.
3
Scenario 2: intentional + no other heir
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, progression is not cut, and qisas is due. Muhammad alone says progression is cut, no qisas.
Source: 'وإن لم يكن له ورثة لا يقطع السراية عندهما خلافا لمحمد'.
4
Scenario 3: mistaken
Emancipation cuts progression by consensus; only decrease in value is due.
Source: 'وإن كان القطع خطأ، فالإعتاق يقطع السراية إجماعا'.
5
Analyze the reasoning for dispute
Muhammad argues that the cause of right changes (ownership to inheritance), creating doubt (shubha). The shaykhayn argue certainty of the master's authority as same person.
Source: 'لاختلاف سبب الولاية' vs. 'التيقن بثبوت الولاية للمولى'.

Key Terms
سراية (sarāyah): Progression of an injury leading to death; the effect of the wound extending over time to cause death.
قصاص (qisās): Retaliation in kind for intentional injury or killing.
اشتباه (ishtibāh): Confusion or doubt as to who holds the right, leading to dropping of qisas.
ولاء (walā'): Patronage; the bond between a freed slave and his former master, which gives the master inheritance rights.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), what is the ruling when a slave's hand is intentionally cut, the master emancipates him, and the slave dies with no other heir?
A) Emancipation cuts progression, no qisas
B) Qisas is obligatory on the cutter
C) Only the decrease in value is due
D) The master must pay diyah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intentional injury to a slave followed by emancipation only cuts progression if there is another heir; otherwise, qisas is due according to the majority of the Sahibayn.

Cutting a Slave's Hand Then Manumission: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sirayah
Ruling on effect of manumission after hand-cutting with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether manumission cuts off sirayah when the slave has no other heirs, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Manumission does not automatically cut off sirayah; the existence of other heirs determines qisas.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq examines a nuanced case: a master cuts his slave's hand, then frees him, and the slave dies. The key question is whether the manumission interrupts the causal chain (sirayah) so that the master escapes qisas. The Hanafi school has an internal split: Sahibayn hold qisas stands when there are no other heirs; Imam Muhammad disagrees.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and variables
Identify: the cutting is either intentional or erroneous, and the slave may or may not have heirs other than the master. The ruling depends on these two factors.
2
Identify consensus points
Find where all agree: For erroneous cutting, manumission cuts off sirayah by consensus regardless of heirs. For intentional cutting with other heirs, also consensus that sirayah is cut off.
Consensus: sirayah is cut off when there are other heirs or when the cutting is erroneous.
3
Locate the dispute
The dispute arises only when the cutting is intentional and the slave has no heirs other than the master. Sahibayn say sirayah is not cut off, so qisas is possible. Muhammad says sirayah is cut off, so no qisas.
Dispute: intentional, no other heirs.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Sahibayn base their view on certainty of the master's authority at both the time of cutting (as owner) and at death (as inheritor by wala). Muhammad argues that the cause of authority differs (ownership vs. inheritance), creating doubt that prevents qisas.
Sahibayn: certainty of authority; Muhammad: difference of cause creates doubt.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) is relied upon: when there are no other heirs, qisas is obligatory. Practically, the master is subject to retaliation; according to Muhammad, he only pays the deficiency value.
Mufta bihi: qisas is executed.

قيمة العبد قطع العبد
منه، وله ورثة غيره لا يقتص، وإلا اقتص منه. سراية القطع للعبد المذكور أي غير السيد أي للقطع بالإجماع
العبد
وفي المغصوب إلخ: أي لو غصب عبدا أو أمة، وقيمته عشرون ألفا، فهلك عند الغاصب، تجب قيمته بالغة ما بلغت بالإجماع؛ لأن الغصب يرد على المال، فكان الواجب بمقابلة المال، فيجب بالغا ما بلغ. (ملا مسكين، عيني) دية الحر إلخ لأن القيمة في العبد كالدية في الحر، فإذا وجب في الحر كل الدية يجب في العبد كل القيمة، وإذا وجب في الحر نصف الدية يجب في العبد نصف القيمة، لكن ليس هذا على إطلاقه، بل إذا لم تبلغ قدر الدية، وأما إذا بلغت فينقص عشرة كما مر. (فتح بتصرف)
ففي يده إلخ: توضيح للحكم المذكور أي إذا كان ما قدر من دية الحر مقدرا من قيمة العبد، ففي قطع يده يجب نصف قيمته؛ لأنا ذكرنا أن القيمة في العبد كالدية في الحر؛ إذ هو بدل الدم فيكون في يده نصف قيمته، لا يزاد على خمسة آلاف إلا خمسة؛ لأن اليد في الآدمي ،نصفه فيعتبر بكله، وينقص هذا المقدار إظهارا لدناءة مرتبته، وقيل: يضمن في الأطراف بحسابه بالغة ما بلغت، ولا ينقص منه شيء؛ لأن الأطراف يسلك فيها مسلك الأموال، وهو قول مالك وأحمد في رواية إلا في الآمة والجائفة والمنقلة والموضحة فيقدر فيها ما يقدر في دية الحر، وهذا أمر شنيع؛ لأنه إذا كانت قيمته مثلا مائة ألف فإنه بقطع يده يجب خمسون ألفا، وبقتله عشرة آلاف إلا عشرة. [ رمز الحقائق ٤٦١/٢] أقول: ما ذكره الشيخ العيني أولا، ورجحه هو الذي جزم به الملتقي، وأخذه في عامة الكتب "كـ الهداية" و"الخلاصة" و"مجمع البحرين" وغيرها، وما ذكره ثانيا وضيفه هو الذي صححه بعضهم، وهو ظاهر الرواية، والتفصيل في "رد المحتار".
قطع يد عبد الخ: اعلم أن قطع يد العبد لا يخلو إما أن يكون عمدا أو خطأ، وكل وجه على وجهين، إما أن يكون للعبد وارث غير السيد أو لم يكن، فإن كان القطع عمدا ووارثه غيره، فالإعتاق يقطع السراية إجماعا، ولا يجب القصاص، وإن لم يكن له ورثة لا يقطع السراية عندهما خلافا لمحمد، وإن كان القطع خطأ، فالإعتاق يقطع
السراية إجماعا، سواء كان له وارث أم لا، ولا تجب القيمة والدية، بل يجب نقصان القيمة بالقطع. (فتح) لا يقتص: أي لا يقتص القاطع بالإجماع؛ لاشتباه من له الحق؛ لأن القصاص يجب عند الموت مستندا إلى وقت الجرح، فعلى اعتبار حالة الجرح يكون الحق للمولى، وعلى اعتبار الحالة الثانية يكون للورثة، فتحقق الاشتباه، فسقط القصاص رمز الحقائق : ٤٦١/٢] وإلا اقتص منه : يعني وإن لم يكن للعبد ورثة غير السيد اقتص منه أي من القاطع عندهما، وقال محمد: لا يجب القصاص هنا أيضا ؛ لاختلاف سبب الولاية؛ لأن الملك على اعتبار حالة الجرح، والوراثة بالولاء على اعتبار حالة الموت فنزل اختلاف السبب منزلة اختلاف المستحق، فتمكنت الشبهة، فسقط القصاص، ولهما التيقن بثبوت الولاية للمولى، فيستوفيه [رمز الحقائق: ٤٦١/٢]
Book of Diyat: And in the female slave: deficiency. 458: Rulings of injury upon the slave: ten out of five thousand. And in the usurped (slave), its value is obligatory whatever it reaches. And what is estimated from the free person's blood-money is estimated from the slave's value, so for his hand half his value. He cut the hand of a slave, then his master emancipated him, then he died. The value of the slave, cutting of the slave... from him, and he has heirs other than the master, he is not subject to retaliation; otherwise, retaliation is exacted from him. The spreading of the cutting for the mentioned slave (i.e., other than the master) i.e., for the cutting, by consensus. And in the usurped etc.: i.e., if someone usurps a male or female slave, and its value is twenty thousand, and it perishes with the usurper, its value is obligatory whatever it reaches, by consensus; because usurpation applies to property, so the obligatory (compensation) is in exchange for property, so it is obligatory whatever it reaches. (Mulla Miskeen, 'Ayni) The free person's blood-money etc.: because the value in the slave is like the blood-money in the free person. So when in the free person the entire blood-money is obligatory, in the slave the entire value is obligatory; and when in the free person half the blood-money is obligatory, in the slave half the value is obligatory. But this is not absolute, rather if it does not reach the amount of blood-money, but if it reaches, it is reduced by ten as passed. (Fath with adaptation) So in his hand etc.: clarification of the mentioned ruling: i.e., if what is estimated from the free person's blood-money is estimated from the slave's value, then for cutting his hand half his value is obligatory; because we mentioned that the value in the slave is like the blood-money in the free person, since it is the substitute for blood, so for his hand half his value is obligatory, not increased beyond five thousand except five; because the hand in a human is half of him, so it is considered by his whole, and this amount is reduced to show the lowness of his rank. And it was said: liability for limbs is proportionally whatever it reaches, and nothing is reduced from it; because limbs are treated as property, and this is the saying of Malik and Ahmad in one narration except for the female slave, and the penetrating wound, and the cranial fracture, and the scalp wound, where it is estimated as estimated in the free person's blood-money. And this is a dreadful thing; because if his value is for example one hundred thousand, then by cutting his hand fifty thousand is obligatory, and by killing him ten thousand minus ten. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/461] I say: what Shaykh al-'Ayni mentioned first and favored is what al-Multaqi affirmed and adopted in most books like al-Hidaya, al-Khulasa, Majma' al-Bahrayn and others, and what he mentioned second and added is what some corrected, and it is the apparent transmission, and the detail is in Radd al-Muhtar. Section: Cutting the hand of a slave etc.: Know that cutting the hand of a slave is either intentional or erroneous, and each aspect has two aspects: either the slave has an heir other than the master or not. If the cutting is intentional and his heir is other (than the master), then manumission cuts off the spreading (of injury) by consensus, and retaliation is not obligatory. If he has no heirs, it does not cut off the spreading according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Muhammad. If the cutting is erroneous, then manumission cuts off the spreading by consensus, whether he has an heir or not, and neither the value nor the blood-money is obligatory, rather the deficiency in value due to the cutting is obligatory. (Fath) He is not subject to retaliation: i.e., the cutter is not subject to retaliation by consensus, due to confusion regarding who has the right; because retaliation becomes obligatory at death based on the time of the wound. Considering the state of the wound, the right belongs to the master; considering the second state, it belongs to the heirs. Thus confusion arises, so retaliation is dropped. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/461] And otherwise retaliation is exacted from him: i.e., if the slave has no heirs other than the master, retaliation is exacted from the cutter according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad said: retaliation is not obligatory here either, due to difference in the cause of authority; because ownership is based on the time of the wound, and inheritance by patronage is based on the time of death. So the difference of cause takes the place of difference of rightful claimant, thus doubt arises and retaliation is dropped. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), there is certainty of established authority for the master, so he executes it. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 2/461]
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of manumission on liability for cutting a slave's hand, followed by the slave's death. The author first establishes the general principle that a slave's value is analogous to a free person's blood-money (diyah), but with a cap: the value for a limb is not increased beyond a certain amount relative to the full value. He then notes a difference with Malik and Ahmad who treat limbs as property without cap. The core ruling: If a master cuts his slave's hand, then emancipates him, and the slave later dies, the rules differ based on whether the cutting was intentional or erroneous, and whether the slave has heirs other than the master. If intentional with other heirs, emancipation cuts off the spreading (sirayah) by consensus, so no retaliation. If intentional with no other heirs, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that retaliation is still possible, but Imam Muhammad disagrees, citing conflicting bases of right (ownership vs. inheritance). If erroneous, emancipation cuts off sirayah by consensus, and only the deficiency in value is due. The commentary explains the reasoning: the confusion of right prevents qisas, but the Sahibayn insist on certainty of the master's authority. This shows how Hanafi usul handles conflicting presumptions in criminal liability.

Key Terms
السراية (al-sirāyah): The spreading of an injury from the initial wound to cause death or further harm, affecting liability.
القصاص (al-qiṣāṣ): Retaliatory punishment, specifically taking life for life or limb for limb.
العتق (al-‘itq): Manumission, the freeing of a slave by the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does manumission cut off sirayah by consensus?
A) Intentional cutting with other heirs
B) Intentional cutting without other heirs
C) Erroneous cutting regardless of heirs
D) Both A and C

Key Takeaway
Manumission cuts off sirayah in accidental cases always, and in intentional cases only when the slave has other heirs; the intra-Hanafi dispute concerns intentional cases without other heirs.

Compensation for Injury by Slaves Before Ambiguous Manumission Clarified
Ruling on compensation when master ambiguously declares one slave free then both injure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation when a master ambiguously declares one slave free and both injure someone before clarification, and explain the reasoning based on the nature of bayan.

Core Idea
Ambiguous freedom declaration does not retroactively remove ownership for injuries occurring before clarification.

This lesson addresses a tricky scenario: a master says 'one of you two slaves is free' but does not specify which. Before he clarifies, both slaves cause a wound to someone. Later, the master indicates which slave was meant. Who gets the compensation? The Hanafi school holds that the master receives compensation for both injuries because the clarification is treated as a creative act (insha') taking effect at the time of clarification, not retroactively. At the time of injury, both slaves were owned, so the master is entitled to the arsh for both. Let's unpack the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous statement
The master says 'one of you two is free' without naming which slave. This creates ambiguity (ibham) regarding the identity of the freed slave.
The statement is not a clear specification of a particular slave.
2
Establish the timing of the injury
The wound (shajjah) occurs after the ambiguous statement but before the master clarifies which slave he intended. This timing is crucial for determining ownership at the moment of injury.
3
Analyze the legal nature of the clarification (bayan)
According to the Hanafi school, the clarification (bayan) of an ambiguous statement can be either a mere disclosure (izhar) or a creative act (insha'). Here, since the freedom takes effect only after clarification, it is considered an insha' – as if the master emancipated at the time of clarification.
Thus, the emancipation is not retroactive. The slave was not free at the time of injury.
4
Apply the principle to compensation
Because both slaves were owned at the time of the wound, the master – as owner – is entitled to the compensation (arsh) for the injuries caused by both slaves. The later clarification does not change this.
Al-Zayla'i adds: emancipation was not fixed on a specific person until the clarification, but the wound attaches to a specific individual, so the slaves remained owned for injury purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أحدكما حر، فشجا، فبين في أحدهما، فأرشهما للسيد. أي أرش العبدين للمولى لأن البيان إظهار من وجه وإنشاء من وجه وبعد الشج يبقى محلا، فاعتبر إنشاء، فكأنه أعتق وقت البيان، كذا في "شرح الملتقى"، وعلله الزيلعي بأن العتق غير نازل في المعين والشجة تصادف المعين، فبقيا مملوكين في حق ا فقاً الشجة. (فتح) عيني عبد إلخ: أي إذا فقأ رجل عيني عبد فالمولى بالخيار إن شاء دفع العبد المفقوء إلى الفاقئ، وأخذ قيمته كاملا، وإن شاء أمسكه، ولا شيء له، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة لله، وقالا: إن شاء أمسك العبد وأخذ ما نقصه، وإن شاء دفع العبد وأخذ قيمته وقال الشافعي يضمنه كل القيمة ويمسك الجثة؛ لأنه يجعل الضمان مقابلا بالفائت، فبقي الباقي على ملكه ولهما: أنه في الجناية بمنزلة المال، فأوجب ذلك تخيير المولى على الوجه الذي قلناه كما في سائر الأموال وله أن المالية وإن كانت معتبرة في الذات، فالآدمية أيضا غير مهدرة فيها وفي أطراف العبد، ولهذا لو قطع عبد يد عبد، يؤمر المولى بالدفع أو الفداء، ولو كان العبد القاطع مالا محضا لوجب أن يباع فيها، ثم من أحكام الآدمية أن لا ينقسم الضمان على الأجزاء يعني الأجزاء الفائتة والقائمة، بل يكون بإزاء الفائتة لا غير ولا يتملك الجثة، ومن أحكام المالية أن ينقسم ويتملك، فوفرنا على الشبهين حظهما فقلنا بأنه لا ينقسم باعتبار الآدمية، ويتملك الجثة باعتبار المالية. (فتح) ضمن السيد إلخ: لما روي عن أبي عبيدة بن الجراح له أنه قضى بجناية المدبر على المولى بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير، وكان يومئذ أميرا بالشام، فكان إجماعا، ولأن المولى صار مانعا بالتدبير والاستيلاد تسليمه في الجناية غير أن يصير مختارا للفداء؛ لعدم علمه بما يحدث، فصار كما إذا فعل ذلك بعد الجناية، وهو لا يعلم، وإنما يجب الأقل منهما؛ لأنه لا حق لولي الجناية في أكثر من الأرش، ولا منع من المولى في أكثر من العين، وقيمتها تقوم مقامها، ولا يخير بين الأقل والأكثر؛ لأنه لا يفيد في جنس واحد؛ لاختياره الأقل. رمز الحقائق: ٤٦٢/٢] واحترز بقوله : " في "جنس" عما لو كان الجاني قنا حيث يتخير بين الدفع والفداء، ولا يجب الأقل؛ لأن فيه فائدة لاختلاف الجنس. Thus in Sharh al-Multaqa. Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: if a master ambiguously declares 'one of you two (slaves) is free', then both slaves cause a wound (shajjah), and later it becomes clear which one was meant to be free, the compensation (arsh) for both wounds goes to the master. The commentary explains the legal reasoning: the declaration of freedom is partly an announcement and partly a creative act (insha'). Since the wound occurred before the clarification, the slave remains owned at the time of injury, so the master is entitled to the compensation. Al-Zayla'i adds that emancipation does not apply to a specific person until clarified, while the wound attaches to a specific individual, so both remain slaves for purposes of the injury. This is a technical ruling showing how ambiguity and retroactive determination affect liability.

Key Terms
الأرش (al-arsh): Compensation for injuries to body parts, less than full blood-money.
البيان (al-bayān): Clarification of an ambiguous statement, here regarding which slave is free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The freed slave's wound compensation goes to himself, the other to the master.
B) Both compensations go to the master because at the time of injury both were owned.
C) The victim receives both compensations directly.
D) The master gets nothing because he created ambiguity.

Key Takeaway
When a master ambiguously declares one slave free, any injury caused by the slaves before clarification is compensated to the master, as the freedom takes effect only upon clarification.
